         <p><a href="/wiki/Beno%C3%AEt_Mandelbrot" title="Beno&icirc;t Mandelbrot" class="mw-redirect">Beno&icirc;t Mandelbrot</a>, MS 1948, Engineering 1949, father of <a href="/wiki/Fractal_geometry" title="Fractal geometry" class="mw-redirect">fractal geometry</a>, namesake of the <a href="/wiki/Mandelbrot_set" title="Mandelbrot set">Mandelbrot set</a></p> 
        </div> 
       </div> </li> 
      <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"> 
       <div style="width: 155px"> 
        <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"> 
         <div style="margin:27.5px auto;">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Frank_Capra.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Frank_Capra.JPG/120px-Frank_Capra.JPG" width="120" height="95" /></a>
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="gallerytext"> 
         <p><a href="/wiki/Frank_Capra" title="Frank Capra">Frank Capra</a>, BS Chemical Engineering 1918 (when Caltech was known as the &quot;Throop Institute&quot;);<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> winner of six <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards" class="mw-redirect">Academy Awards</a> in directing and producing; producer and director of <i><a href="/wiki/It%27s_a_Wonderful_Life" title="It's a Wonderful Life">It's a Wonderful Life</a></i></p> 
        </div> 
       </div> </li> 
      <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"> 
       <div style="width: 155px"> 
        <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"> 
         <div style="margin:15px auto;">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kip_Thorne_at_Caltech.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Kip_Thorne_at_Caltech.jpg/94px-Kip_Thorne_at_Caltech.jpg" width="94" height="120" /></a>
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="gallerytext"> 
         <p><a href="/wiki/Kip_Thorne" title="Kip Thorne">Kip Thorne</a>, BS 1962, known for his prolific contributions in gravitation physics and astrophysics and co-founding of <a href="/wiki/LIGO" title="LIGO">LIGO</a></p> 
        </div> 
       </div> </li> 
      <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"> 
       <div style="width: 155px"> 
        <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"> 
         <div style="margin:15px auto;">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Stephen_Wolfram_PR.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Stephen_Wolfram_PR.jpg/84px-Stephen_Wolfram_PR.jpg" width="84" height="120" /></a>
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="gallerytext"> 
         <p><a href="/wiki/Stephen_Wolfram" title="Stephen Wolfram">Stephen Wolfram</a>, PhD 1979, creator of <a href="/wiki/Mathematica" title="Mathematica">Mathematica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wolfram_Alpha" title="Wolfram Alpha">Wolfram Alpha</a>; one of the first <a href="/wiki/MacArthur_Fellows" title="MacArthur Fellows" class="mw-redirect">MacArthur Fellows</a> in 1981</p> 
        </div> 
       </div> </li> 
      <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"> 
       <div style="width: 155px"> 
        <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"> 
         <div style="margin:15px auto;">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Stanislav_Smirnov.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Stanislav_Smirnov.jpg/73px-Stanislav_Smirnov.jpg" width="73" height="120" /></a>
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="gallerytext"> 
         <p><a href="/wiki/Stanislav_Smirnov" title="Stanislav Smirnov">Stanislav Smirnov</a>, PhD 1996, 2010 <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields Medal</a> winner for his work on the mathematical foundations of <a href="/wiki/Statistical_physics" title="Statistical physics">statistical physics</a>, particularly finite lattice models</p> 
        </div> 
       </div> </li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Presidents">Presidents</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=California_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Presidents">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/James_Augustin_Brown_Scherer" title="James Augustin Brown Scherer">James Augustin Brown Scherer</a> (1908?1920) (president of Throop College of Technology before the name change)</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Robert_A._Millikan" title="Robert A. Millikan" class="mw-redirect">Robert A. Millikan</a> (1921?1945), experimental physicist, Nobel laureate in physics for 1923 (his official title was &quot;Chairman of the Executive Council&quot;)</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Lee_A._DuBridge" title="Lee A. DuBridge" class="mw-redirect">Lee A. DuBridge</a> (1946?1969), experimental physicist (first to officially hold the title of President)</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Harold_Brown_(Secretary_of_Defense)" title="Harold Brown (Secretary of Defense)">Harold Brown</a> (1969?1977), physicist and public servant (left Caltech to serve as <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Defense" title="United States Secretary of Defense">United States Secretary of Defense</a> in the administration of <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Carter" title="Jimmy Carter">Jimmy Carter</a>)</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Christy" title="Robert F. Christy">Robert F. Christy</a> (1977?1978), astrophysicist (acting president)</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Marvin_L._Goldberger" title="Marvin L. Goldberger" class="mw-redirect">Marvin L. Goldberger</a> (1978?1987), theoretical physicist (left to serve as Director of <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Advanced_Studies" title="Institute for Advanced Studies" class="mw-redirect">Institute for Advanced Studies</a>)</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Thomas_E._Everhart" title="Thomas E. Everhart" class="mw-redirect">Thomas E. Everhart</a> (1987?1997), experimental physicist</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/David_Baltimore" title="David Baltimore">David Baltimore</a> (1997?2006), molecular biologist, Nobel laureate in physiology or medicine for 1975</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Jean-Lou_Chameau" title="Jean-Lou Chameau">Jean-Lou Chameau</a> (2006?2013), civil engineer and educational administrator (leaving to serve as President of <a href="/wiki/KAUST" title="KAUST" class="mw-redirect">KAUST</a>)</li> 
     </ul> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_media_and_popular_culture">In media and popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=California_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: In media and popular culture">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>Caltech has appeared in many works of popular culture, both as itself and in disguised form. <a href="/wiki/MIT_in_popular_culture" title="MIT in popular culture">As with MIT</a>, a Caltech reference is often used to establish a character's high level of intelligence or a technical background. For example, on television, the four male lead characters of the sitcom <i><a href="/wiki/The_Big_Bang_Theory" title="The Big Bang Theory">The Big Bang Theory</a></i> are all employed at the Institute. Caltech is also the inspiration, and frequent film location, for the California Institute of Science of <i><a href="/wiki/Numb3rs" title="Numb3rs" class="mw-redirect">Numb3rs</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-realgenius_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-realgenius-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> On film, the Pacific Tech of <i><a href="/wiki/The_War_of_the_Worlds_(1953_film)" title="The War of the Worlds (1953 film)">The War of the Worlds</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-cowan_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cowan-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Real_Genius" title="Real Genius">Real Genius</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-realgenius_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-realgenius-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> is based on Caltech. In nonfiction, two 2007 documentaries examine aspects of Caltech; <i>Curious</i>, its researchers,<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> and <i>Quantum Hoops</i>, its men's basketball team.</p> 
     <p>Given its Los Angeles-area location, the grounds of the Institute are often host to short scenes in movies and television. The <a href="/wiki/Athenaeum_at_Caltech" title="Athenaeum at Caltech">Athenaeum dining club</a> appears in the <a href="/wiki/Beverly_Hills_Cop_(film_series)" title="Beverly Hills Cop (film series)" class="mw-redirect"><i>Beverly Hills Cop</i> series</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_X-Files_(film)" title="The X-Files (film)">The X-Files</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/True_Romance" title="True Romance">True Romance</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_West_Wing" title="The West Wing">The West Wing</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

       <li id="cite_note-121"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-121">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">&quot;In 1998, Celestis, at the request of NASA, provided a Luna Flight Capsule to the family and friends of the late legendary astronomer and planetary geologist Eugene Shoemaker. The Celestis Flight Capsule, containing a symbolic portion of Shoemaker's cremated remains, was attached to NASA's Lunar Prospector spacecraft and launched on a one-year mission orbiting the moon. On July 31, 1999, at the completion of Lunar Prospector's mission, the spacecraft was intentionally crashed into the moon's south pole, making Shoemaker the first human to be laid to rest on another celestial body. NASA called the memorial &quot;a special honor for a special human being.&quot;&quot;<span class="citation web">Clara Moskowitz (March 28, 2008). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.space.com/news/080328-moon-burial.html">&quot;Fly Me to the Moon...Forever&quot;</a>. <a href="/wiki/Space.com" title="Space.com">Space.com</a>.</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACalifornia+Institute+of+Technology&amp;rft.au=Clara+Moskowitz&amp;rft.aulast=Clara+Moskowitz&amp;rft.btitle=Fly+Me+to+the+Moon...Forever&amp;rft.date=March+28%2C+2008&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.space.com%2Fnews%2F080328-moon-burial.html&amp;rft.pub=Space.com&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&nbsp;</span></span></span></li>

       <li id="cite_note-131"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-131">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">&quot;How he was miserable is more complicated than even I could get into a hundred thousand word book. There was something wrong with him. What was wrong with him, we don't really know. He was at best paranoid. He was probably obsessive-compulsive. The manuscript of the book has been shown to about six or seven psychotherapist, and I asked them for a diagnosis, and they came back with six or seven different diagnoses.&quot; <span class="citation web"><a href="/wiki/Ira_Flatow" title="Ira Flatow">Ira Flatow</a> (interview) with journalist Joel Shurkin (July 21, 2006). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.npr.org/templates/story/story.php?storyId=5573656">&quot;Electronics Pioneer William Shockley's Legacy&quot;</a>. <a href="/wiki/National_Public_Radio" title="National Public Radio" class="mw-redirect">National Public Radio</a>.</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACalifornia+Institute+of+Technology&amp;rft.au=Ira+Flatow+%28interview%29+with+journalist+Joel+Shurkin&amp;rft.aulast=Ira+Flatow+%28interview%29+with+journalist+Joel+Shurkin&amp;rft.btitle=Electronics+Pioneer+William+Shockley%27s+Legacy&amp;rft.date=July+21%2C+2006&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.npr.org%2Ftemplates%2Fstory%2Fstory.php%3FstoryId%3D5573656&amp;rft.pub=National+Public+Radio&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&nbsp;</span></span></span></li> 
       <li id="cite_note-132"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-132">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">&quot;Shockley, whose role as coinventor of the transistor would win him a share of the 1956 Nobel Prize in physics, succeeded in luring a diverse group of accomplished scientists, including Moore, to the Shockley Semiconductor Laboratory, in Palo Alto, California. He then proceeded to antagonize and alienate enough of them to inspire an exodus.&quot;<span class="citation web">Hillary Bhaskaran (2002 (from Volume 36, Number 2)). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://pr.caltech.edu/periodicals/caltechnews/articles/v36/moore.html">&quot;Calibrating Gordon Moore&quot;</a>.        <li id="cite_note-133"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-133">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">&quot;Joel Shurnkin: ...He decided he was going to be the first entrepreneur of the electronic age, and indeed he was. With backing from a man named <a href="/wiki/Arnold_O._Beckman" title="Arnold O. Beckman" class="mw-redirect">Arnold Beckman</a>, he founded Shockley Semiconductor in Palo Alto and he was going to build ? at least at first he was going to build silicon transistors. It was his decision that they use <a href="/wiki/Silicon" title="Silicon">silicon</a> as opposed to <a href="/wiki/Germanium" title="Germanium">germanium</a>, otherwise we'd be talking about Germanium Valley out there instead of Silicon Valley. (Soundbite of laughter) &quot;<span class="citation web"><a href="/wiki/Ira_Flatow" title="Ira Flatow">Ira Flatow</a> (interview) with journalist Joel Shurkin (July 21, 2006). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.npr.org/templates/story/story.php?storyId=5573656">&quot;Electronics Pioneer William Shockley's Legacy ?
